Logic and Technical Terms
intermediate
6 min
Truth and Falsehood: Correspondence with Reality
Sanusi defines lying, gives two examples, and argues for the Sunni definition's importance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni definition of truth and falsehood as correspondence with reality, and why it is crucial for certainty in prophetic reports.

Core Idea
Truth is correspondence with reality, not just belief — securing the Prophet's reliability.

Sanusi begins by defining lying as the non-correspondence of a report with reality, not merely with the speaker's belief. He then provides two contrasting examples to illustrate how this definition works in practice. Finally, he explains why this definition is essential for trusting the Prophet's messages about the unseen, contrasting it with the Mu'tazili view.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of lying
Read Sanusi's definition carefully: lying is the non-correspondence of a report with what is in reality. Notice that it does not depend on the speaker's belief.
The definition is absolute — it does not consider intention or belief.
2
Examine the two examples
Read both examples: the Mu'tazili who believes a false statement, and the Sunni who states the same falsehood under duress. Both are lies because they do not match reality, regardless of belief.
The second example shows that even a permissible lie remains a lie, but is excused due to necessity.
3
Understand the significance for prophecy
Read the concluding argument: the Sunni definition gives certainty that the Prophet's reports correspond to reality directly, not just to his belief. This is essential for trusting his teachings about the unseen.
Contrast this with the Mu'tazili definition, which would allow for possible discrepancy between report and reality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[ حد الكذب ]
قوله : ( والكذبُ : عدم مطابقة الخبر لما في نفس الأمر ... ) إلى آخره
مثالُ الكذب الذي يوافق الاعتقاد : قولُ المعتزلي : الحيوانُ المختارُ مُوجِدٌ لأفعالِهِ الاختياريَّةِ بالقدرةِ التي خلق الله تعالى لهُ ؛ فَإِنَّ هذا الخبر كذبٌ ؛ لمخالفتِهِ لما في نفس الأمرِ ؛ لأنَّ العقل والنقلَ مِنَ الكتاب والسنَّةِ وإجماع السلف الصالح قبل ظهورِ البدع. . شاهدة أنَّ جميع الكائناتِ خَلْقٌ لمولانا تبارك وتعالى ، ولا شريكَ معَهُ في أثرِ مِنَ الآثار ، والقدريَّةُ مجوس هذه الأمَّةِ يعتقدون خلاف هذا ، وأنَّ الحيوانات هي المستقلة بإيجاد أفعالها الاختياريَّة ؛ بما خلق الله تعالى لها مِنَ القدرة .
ومثالُ الكذب الذي يخالفُ الاعتقاد : هذا الخبرُ بعينِهِ إِذا صدرَ مِنْ سنّي أخبرَ بهِ بمحضر المعتزلةِ سَتْراً لحاله ؛ للخوف منهم ، فَإِنَّهُ وإِنْ كانَ كذباً لمخالفته لما في نفس الأمر فهو مخالف أيضاً لاعتقادِ السنّي الذي أخبرَ بهِ ، للكنَّه ارتكب هذا الكذبَ المباحَ لدعوى الضرورة إليه
ومِنْ ذلكَ : مَنْ يُكرَهُ على النطق بكلمة الكفر وقلبه مطمئن بالإيمان .
دقة وتحري أهل السنة في حد الصدق والكذب واعلم : أنَّ تفسير أهلِ الحقِّ للصدق والكذب حصلَ بهِ الوثوقُ بأخبار الرسول عليه الصلاةُ والسلامُ في أحكامه ووعده ووعيده (1) وأحوال الآخرة جملةً وتفصيلاً ؛ لأنَّا نعلم بالبرهان القطعي صدقه ؛ أي : مطابقة أخبارِهِ لما في نفس الأمر ، لا لاعتقاده فقط معَ جواز مخالفتِها لما في نفس الأمرِ ، وبالله تعالى التوفيق .
(1) إذ لو تم اعتماد تعريف المعتزلة - ولا سيما النظام - الملتفت للنسبة الذهنية دون اعتبار الخارج .. لكانت الأخبار الشرعية قاصرة على الحكم الذهني فقط ، ويحتمل مخالفتها للواقع عندهم ، وهذا من تدقيقات وتحقيقات أئمة أهل السنة ، فما أخبر به الأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام مطابق ابتداءً لما في الواقع ، وبالضرورة لما في أذهانهم
[The definition of lying]
His statement: (And lying is: the non-correspondence of the report with what is in reality ...) to its end.
An example of lying that agrees with belief: the statement of the Mu'tazili: 'The free-acting animal is the originator of its voluntary actions by the power that Allah Almighty created for it'; for this report is a lie due to its opposition to what is in reality; because the intellect and transmitted evidence from the Book and the Sunnah and the consensus of the righteous predecessors before the emergence of innovations all testify that all created things are the creation of our Lord, Blessed and Exalted, and there is no partner with Him in any effect, and the Qadariyya are the Magians of this Ummah who believe contrary to this, and that animals are independent in originating their voluntary actions by the power that Allah Almighty created for them.
And an example of lying that opposes belief: this same report when it issues from a Sunni who reports it in the presence of the Mu'tazila to conceal his state out of fear of them; for although it is a lie due to its opposition to what is in reality, it also opposes the belief of the Sunni who reported it, but he committed this permissible lie because of necessity for it.
And from that: one who is compelled to utter a word of disbelief while his heart is tranquil with faith.
The precision and verification of Ahl al-Sunnah in the definition of truth and falsehood. And know: that the interpretation of the people of truth concerning truth and falsehood results in trust in the reports of the Messenger, upon him blessings and peace, in his rulings, his promise, his threat, and the conditions of the Hereafter in general and in detail; because we know with decisive proof his truthfulness; that is: the correspondence of his reports with what is in reality, not [based on] his belief alone with the possibility of their opposition to what is in reality. And with Allah Almighty is success.
(1) For if the definition of the Mu'tazila – especially al-Nazzam – that turns to the mental relation without considering the external were adopted, then the religious reports would be confined to mental judgment only, and their opposition to reality would be possible according to them. And this is from the fine points and investigations of the imams of Ahl al-Sunnah. For what the prophets, upon them blessings and peace, reported corresponds initially to what is in reality, and necessarily to what is in their minds.
Source pages p. 274

Commentary
This passage defines lying and truthfulness from the Sunni perspective, provides illustrative examples, and argues why this definition is crucial for certainty in prophetic reports. The author begins by giving the definition of lying as the non-correspondence of a report with reality (not merely with the speaker's belief). Two examples follow. The first example is lying that agrees with the speaker's belief: a Mu'tazili says that an animal creates its own actions by the power Allah gave it. This report is a lie because it contradicts reality, even though the Mu'tazili believes it. The author supports this by noting that reason, revelation, and early consensus affirm that all things are created by Allah alone, and those who disagree (the Qadariyya) are likened to Magians. The second example is lying that also opposes the speaker's belief: a Sunni, fearing the Mu'tazila, repeats the same statement to conceal his true position. This report is a lie both because it contradicts reality and because it contradicts his own belief, but it is permissible due to duress, analogous to one forced to utter disbelief while his heart is firm in faith. The author then shifts to the Sunni definition of truthfulness as correspondence with reality, not merely with the speaker's belief. He argues that this definition gives confidence in the Prophet's reports about rulings, promises, threats, and the hereafter, because we know through decisive proof that his reports correspond to reality directly, not just to his belief. The footnote reinforces this by contrasting the Mu'tazili definition (mental correspondence only), which would leave open the possibility that prophetic reports might not match reality, undermining certainty. Thus, the Sunni definition preserves the reliability of divine communication.

Key Terms
الصدق
الكذب
مطابقة الخبر
الاعتقاد
المعتزلة
القدريّة
أهل السنة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Many think that truth and falsehood depend on the speaker's belief: if you believe something, it is true for you; if you don't, it is false.
Correction: The Sunni definition holds that truth is correspondence with objective reality, not with belief. A statement is true only if it matches reality, regardless of what the speaker thinks.

Checkpoint
In the first example of lying in the text, why is the Mu'tazili's statement considered a lie even though he believes it?
A) Because it contradicts the belief of the speaker.
B) Because it does not correspond to what is in reality.
C) Because it was uttered under duress.
D) Because it contradicts the consensus of the Mu'tazila.

Key Takeaway
The Sunni definition of truth as correspondence with reality ensures that the Prophet's reports are unconditionally reliable.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you speak about your faith to others—whether in da‘wah or in casual conversation—do you intentionally align your words with actual reality (what Allah has revealed and what is true about the world), or do you sometimes bend the truth to make Islam more appealing or to avoid awkwardness? How would embracing the Sunni definition of truth change the way you speak about your religion starting today?
?
The passage warns that if truth were merely a matter of belief, then the Prophet’s reports could theoretically be false. Have you ever treated any hadith or Qur’anic statement as ‘symbolic’ or ‘metaphorical’ simply because its literal meaning feels uncomfortable or hard to implement? What would it mean to commit yourself to the fact that every prophetic report corresponds exactly to external reality—and how should that change your obedience today?
?
Consider the example of the Sunni who lied under fear. Are there times in your life where you have distorted the truth out of fear of people’s opinions, social rejection, or personal loss? How does knowing that truth is defined by reality—not by your circumstances or feelings—challenge you to be truthful even when it costs you something?

Logic and Technical Terms
beginner
5 min
Truthfulness as Objective Correspondence
Defines sidq as correspondence with reality and contrasts with Mu'tazilite view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ahl al-Sunna's definition of truthfulness as correspondence with objective reality and how it differs from the Mu'tazilite view based on subjective belief.

Core Idea
Truthfulness is about matching reality, not just sincerity.

This lesson introduces a foundational kalam concept: what does it truly mean for a prophet to be truthful? The Ahl al-Sunna define truthfulness as correspondence with objective reality (nafs al-amr), not merely conformity to the speaker's belief. This distinction is crucial for trusting prophetic reports about the unseen world, and it directly refutes the Mu'tazilite view, particularly that of al-Nazzam, which grounds truth only in mental relation. Read the passage to see how this argument unfolds.

Guided Path
1
Read the Ahl al-Sunna definition
Start with the main text where truthfulness is defined as correspondence of reports to 'what is in reality' (nafs al-amr). Note how this is linked to trust in the Prophet's words.
The author emphasizes that this is established by decisive proof (burhan qat'i).
2
Identify the contrast with Mu'tazilites
In the footnote, the author explains the Mu'tazilite view that truthfulness is merely conformity to the speaker's belief, without requiring alignment with external reality.
Pay attention to the name al-Nazzam and his focus on 'mental relation' (nisba dhihniyya).
3
Understand the consequence of the wrong view
Consider why the Mu'tazilite definition is problematic: if truth is only mental, then prophetic reports might not correspond to actual reality, undermining trust.
This is a precise investigation of Ahl al-Sunna imams.
4
Reflect on the certainty of prophetic reports
The passage concludes that prophets' reports are initially in accordance with reality and necessarily in accordance with their own minds, highlighting the harmony between belief and reality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم : أنَّ تفسيرَ أهلِ الحقِّ للصدق والكذب حصلَ بهِ الوثوقُ بأخبار الرسول عليه الصلاةُ والسلامُ في أحكامه ووعده ووعيده وأحوال الآخرة جملةً وتفصيلاً ؛ لأنَّا نعلم بالبرهان القطعي صدقه ؛ أي : مطابقة أخبارِهِ لما في نفس الأمر ، لا لاعتقاده فقط معَ جواز مخالفتِها لما في نفس الأمرِ ، وبالله تعالى التوفيق . (1) إذ لو تم اعتماد تعريف المعتزلة - ولا سيما النظام - الملتفت للنسبة الذهنية دون اعتبار الخارج .. لكانت الأخبار الشرعية قاصرة على الحكم الذهني فقط ، ويحتمل مخالفتها للواقع عندهم ، وهذا من تدقيقات وتحقيقات أئمة أهل السنة ، فما أخبر به الأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام مطابق ابتداءً لما في الواقع ، وبالضرورة لما في أذهانهم
Know that the interpretation of Ahl al-Haqq (the people of truth) concerning truthfulness (sidq) and falsehood (kadhib) has established trust in the reports of the Messenger (peace and blessings be upon him) regarding his rulings, his promise, his threat, and the states of the afterlife in general and in detail; because we know by decisive proof (burhan qat'i) his truthfulness, i.e., the correspondence of his reports to what is in the mind-independent reality (nafs al-amr), not merely his belief (i'tiqad) while allowing them to contradict what is in reality. And with Allah Almighty is success. (1) For if the definition of the Mu'tazilites - especially al-Nazzam - were adopted, which turns on mental relation without considering external reality, then the religious reports would be confined to mental judgment only, and it would be possible for them to contradict reality according to them. This is among the precise investigations of the imams of Ahl al-Sunna. So what the prophets (peace and blessings be upon them) have reported is initially in accordance with reality, and necessarily in accordance with their own minds.
Source pages p. 275

Commentary
This passage defines truthfulness (sidq) and falsehood (kadhib) according to Ahl al-Sunna and refutes the Mu'tazilite definition. The author begins by stating that the correct interpretation ensures trust in the Prophet's reports (peace be upon him) concerning his rulings, promises, threats, and details of the afterlife. The reason is that we know by decisive proof (burhan qat'i) his truthfulness. The definition of truthfulness is that his reports correspond to what is in objective reality (nafs al-amr), not merely that they conform to his own belief while it would be possible for them to contradict reality. Then the author adds a footnote: if the Mu'tazilite definition were adopted—especially that of al-Nazzam which focuses on mental relation without considering the external—then religious reports would be limited to mental judgments only, and it would be possible for them to contradict reality. This is a precise investigation of the imams of Ahl al-Sunna. The prophets' reports are initially in accordance with reality and necessarily also in accordance with their own minds (i.e., their belief and the reality are necessarily aligned).

Key Terms
sidq
kadhib
nafs al-amr
burhan qat'i
i'tiqad
mu'tazila
nazzam

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That truthfulness is merely being sincere or consistent with one's own beliefs, regardless of whether those beliefs match external reality.
Correction: Ahl al-Sunna emphasize that true truthfulness (sidq) requires that the report actually corresponds to the way things are in objective reality (nafs al-amr), not just the speaker's subjective conviction.

Checkpoint
According to Ahl al-Sunna as explained in the passage, what does truthfulness (sidq) consist in?
A) Conformity with the speaker's belief
B) Correspondence with objective reality (nafs al-amr)
C) Absence of contradiction in the speaker's statements
D) Agreement with the majority of scholars

Key Takeaway
Truthfulness in the Ahl al-Sunna tradition means that a report must correspond to how things actually are in reality, not just to the speaker's internal conviction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If truthfulness is not just about your sincere belief but must match objective reality, then consider: Are you willing to examine your deepest convictions about Allah and the afterlife against the objective standard of revelation, even if it means admitting you've been wrong? What action will you take this week to test your beliefs against the Quran and Sunnah?
?
The Mu'tazilite definition would allow a prophet's report to contradict reality as long as he believes it. Do you sometimes treat your own understanding of the deen as sufficient simply because you feel strongly about it, neglecting to check whether it aligns with the actual texts? Ask yourself: In what area of your life are you operating based on your own feelings rather than submission to what Allah has actually revealed?
?
This lesson says that prophetic reports are initially in accordance with reality. When you read a hadith that challenges your desires or intellect, do you submit to its objective truth or do you reinterpret it to fit your own mental framework? What is one report you struggle with, and what would it look like for you to accept it as corresponding to reality exactly as it is?
